srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ellipse_sign_200.svg/47px-Ellipse_sign_200.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ellipse_sign_200.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_200.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="192" /></a></span> <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_201" title="Puerto Rico Highway 201"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ellipse_sign_201.svg/31px-Ellipse_sign_201.svg.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ellipse_sign_201.svg/47px-Ellipse_sign_201.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ellipse_sign_201.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_201.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="192" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Vieques</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="noprint"><span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\\/\\/upload.wikimedia.org\\/wikipedia\\/commons\\/transcoded\\/5\\/57\\/En-us-Vieques_from_Puerto_Rico_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg\\/En-us-Vieques_from_Puerto_Rico_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;En-us-Vieques from Puerto Rico pronunciation (Voice of America).ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/57/En-us-Vieques_from_Puerto_Rico_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg/En-us-Vieques_from_Puerto_Rico_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Vieques_from_Puerto_Rico_pronunciation_(Voice_of_America).ogg" title="File:En-us-Vieques from Puerto Rico pronunciation (Voice of America).ogg">\xe2\x93\x98</a></sup></span></span></span>; <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xcb\x88bjekes&#93;</a></span>), officially <b>Isla de Vieques</b>, is an island, <a href="/wiki/Culebra_barrio-pueblo" title="Culebra barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, and together with <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>, it is geographically part of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Virgin_Islands" title="Spanish Virgin Islands">Spanish Virgin Islands</a>. Vieques lies about 8 miles (13&#160;km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Geography of Puerto Rico">mainland of Puerto Rico</a>, measuring about 20 miles (32&#160;km) long and 4.5 miles (7&#160;km) wide. Its most populated <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrio</a> is the town of <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Segunda,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabel Segunda, Puerto Rico">Isabel Segunda</a> (or "Isabel the Second", sometimes written "Isabel II"), the administrative center located on the northern side of the island. The population of Vieques was 8,249 at the 2020 Census.\n</p><p>The island\'s name is a Spanish spelling of a <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word said to mean "small island" or "small land". It also has the nickname <i>Isla Nena</i>, usually translated as "girl island" or "little girl island", alluding to its perception as Puerto Rico\'s little sister. The island was given this name by the Puerto Rican poet <a href="/wiki/Luis_Llorens_Torres" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Llorens Torres">Lu\xc3\xads Llor\xc3\xa9ns Torres</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">British colonial</a> period, its name was <b>Crab Island</b>.\n</p><p>Vieques is best known internationally as the site of a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_in_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="United States Navy in Vieques, Puerto Rico">series of protests</a>, held against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>\'s use of the island as a <a href="/wiki/Bombing_range" title="Bombing range">bombing range</a> and testing-ground, leading to the Navy\'s departure in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, the former navy lands are a <a href="/wiki/Vieques_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Vieques National Wildlife Refuge">national wildlife refuge</a>; some of it is open to the public, but much remains closed off due to biological or chemical contamination or <a href="/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance" title="Unexploded ordnance">unexploded ordnance</a> that the military is, slowly, cleaning up.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the most beautiful beaches on the island are on the eastern end (former site of the Marine Base) that the Navy named Red Beach, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Beach_(Vieques)" title="Blue Beach (Vieques)">Blue Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Beach_(Vieques)" title="Caracas Beach (Vieques)">Caracas Beach</a>, Pata Prieta Beach, La Chiva Beach, and Plata Beach. At the far western tip (formerly the Navy Base) is <a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas,_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Punta Arenas, Vieques, Puerto Rico">Punta Arenas</a>, which the Navy named \'Green Beach\'. The beaches are commonly listed among the top in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> for their azure waters and white sands.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pre-Columbian_history">Pre-Columbian history</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Archaeological evidence suggests that Vieques was first inhabited by ancient Indigenous peoples of the Americas who traveled mostly from South America perhaps between 3000 BCE and 2000 BCE. Estimates of these prehistoric dates of inhabitation vary widely. These tribes had a <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> culture and were probably fishermen and <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>.\n</p><p>Excavations at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ferro" title="Puerto Ferro">Puerto Ferro</a> site by Luis Chanlatte and Yvonne Narganes<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> uncovered a fragmented human skeleton in a large hearth area. Radiocarbon dating of shells found in the hearth indicate a burial date of c. 1900 BCE. This skeleton, popularly known as <i>El Hombre de Puerto Ferro</i>, was buried at the center of a group of large boulders near Vieques\'s south-central coast, approximately one kilometer northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Mosquito" title="Puerto Mosquito">Bioluminescent Bay</a>. Linear arrays of smaller stones radiating from the central boulders are apparent at the site today, but their age and reason for placement are unknown.\n</p><p>Further waves of settlement by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> followed over many centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawak</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Igneri" title="Igneri">Igneri</a>) people, thought to have originated in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, arrived in the region perhaps around 200 BC (estimates vary). These tribes, noted for their pottery, stone carving, and other artifacts, eventually merged with groups from <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> to form what is now called the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> culture. This culture flourished in the region from around 1000 AD until the arrival of <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">Europeans</a> in the late 15th century.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spanish_colonial_period">Spanish colonial period</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Spanish colonial period"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The European discovery of Vieques is sometimes credited to <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, who landed in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> in 1493. It does not seem to be certain whether Columbus personally visited Vieques, but in any case the island was soon claimed by the Spanish. During the early 16th century Vieques became a center of Ta\xc3\xadno rebellion against the European invaders, prompting the Spanish to send armed forces to the island to quell the resistance. The native Ta\xc3\xadno population was decimated, and its people either killed, imprisoned or enslaved by the Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-Historic_Resources_UFDC_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historic_Resources_UFDC-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Spanish did not, however, permanently colonize Vieques at this time, and for the next 300 years it remained a lawless outpost, frequented by <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a> and outlaws. As European powers fought for control in the region, a series of attempts by the <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Danish colonization of the Americas">Danish</a> to colonize the island in the 17th and 18th centuries were repulsed by the Spanish.\n</p><p>At the beginning of the 19th century, the Spanish took steps to permanently settle and secure the island. In 1811, Don Salvador Mel\xc3\xa9ndez, then governor of Puerto Rico, sent military commander Juan Rossell\xc3\xb3 to begin what would become the annexation of Vieques by the Puerto Ricans.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1832, under an agreement with the Spanish Puerto Rican administration, Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Jos%C3%A9_Jaime_Mar%C3%ADa_Le_Guillou" title="Te\xc3\xb3filo Jos\xc3\xa9 Jaime Mar\xc3\xada Le Guillou">Te\xc3\xb3filo Jos\xc3\xa9 Jaime Mar\xc3\xada Le Guillou</a> became Governor of Vieques, and undertook to impose order on the anarchic province. He was instrumental in the establishment of large plantations, marking a period of social and economic change. Le Guillou is now remembered as the <i>founder of Vieques</i> (though this title is also sometimes conferred on Francisco Sa\xc3\xadnz, governor from 1843 to 1852, who founded <a href="/wiki/Isabel_II_barrio-pueblo" title="Isabel II barrio-pueblo">Isabel Segunda</a>, the main town in Vieques, named after <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabella II of Spain">Queen Isabel II</a> of Spain). Vieques was formally annexed to Puerto Rico in 1854.\n</p><p>In 1816, Vieques was briefly visited by <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Sim\xc3\xb3n Bol\xc3\xadvar">Sim\xc3\xb3n Bol\xc3\xadvar</a> when his ship ran aground there while fleeing defeat in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>During the second part of the 19th century, thousands of slaves of African descent were brought to Vieques to work the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">sugarcane plantations</a>. They arrived from mainland Puerto Rico and nearby islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">St. Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a>, and many other Caribbean islands. Slavery was abolished in Puerto Rico in 1873.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="European_colonial_period">European colonial period</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European colonial period"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The island also received considerable attention as a possible colony from <a href="/wiki/Scottish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Scottish colonization of the Americas">Scotland</a>, and after numerous attempts to buy the island proved unsuccessful, the Scottish fleet, en route to <a href="/wiki/Darien_scheme" title="Darien scheme">Darien</a> in 1698, made landfall and took possession of the island in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Scotland" title="Company of Scotland">Company of Scotland Trading to Africa and The Indies</a>. Scottish sovereignty of the island proved short-lived, as a Danish ship arrived shortly afterward and claimed the island. From 1689 to 1693, the island was controlled by <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussia</a> as <b>Krabbeninsel</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> <i>crab island</i>), where the English name Crab Island came from.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_States_control">United States control</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: United States control"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vieques,_PR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Vieques%2C_PR.jpg/220px-Vieques%2C_PR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="390" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Vieques%2C_PR.jpg/330px-Vieques%2C_PR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Vieques%2C_PR.jpg/440px-Vieques%2C_PR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Municipio de Vieques plaque</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Puerto Rico was ceded by Spain in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the United States conducted its first census of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Vieques was 6,642 (but this included 704 residents from a nearby island, <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1920s and 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_industry" title="Sugar industry">sugar industry</a>, on which Vieques was dependent, went into decline due to falling prices and industrial unrest. Many locals were forced to move to mainland Puerto Rico or <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a> to look for work.\n</p><p>In 1941, while Europe was in the midst of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> purchased or seized almost eighty percent<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> of Vieques as an extension to the <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Roads_Naval_Station" title="Roosevelt Roads Naval Station">Roosevelt Roads Naval Station</a> nearby on the Puerto Rican mainland. It is said that the original purpose of the base (never implemented) was to provide a safe haven for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British fleet</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_royal_family" title="British royal family">British royal family</a> should Great Britain fall to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This assertion does not match U.S. Navy documents and the obvious fact that Canada\'s <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Harbour" title="Halifax Harbour">Halifax harbor</a> would have been a more likely fallback position for the British fleet, with British King <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> already reigning as King of Canada. The base was however seen as the Atlantic\'s counterpart of <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> due to its strategic location. The Naval Station at Roosevelt Roads was a perfect location to defend the strategic approaches to the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a>.\n</p><p>Much of the land was bought from the owners of large farms and sugar cane plantations, and the expropriations triggered the final demise of the sugar industry. Without consulting the local population who had lived and worked there for centuries and protested the expropriations,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the decision to turn it into a bombing range was made in Washington. In a similar way as the <a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">former population</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Islands</a>, who were displaced to make way for an Air Force Base in the Indian Ocean in the 1960s, many agricultural workers, who had no formal title to the land they occupied, were evicted and forced to migrate.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>For over sixty years, the US military used the island (with a population of over 9000 inhabitants in 1950<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) as a live munitions target practice. According to internal Navy documents, bombardments occurred on 180 days out of a year on average. The US military used the highest possible contaminant <a href="/wiki/Depleted_uranium" title="Depleted uranium">depleted uranium</a> (DU) munitions since 1972 on the populated (and full of exotic wildlife) island, at a rate of over 80 live bombs daily for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The health consequences are felt to this day as the cancer rates are ostensibly higher for the population of Vieques, especially children, than for those on the main island.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>After the war, the US Navy continued to use the island for military exercises, and as a firing range and testing ground for <a href="/wiki/Munitions" class="mw-redirect" title="Munitions">munitions</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Protests_and_departure_of_the_United_States_Navy">Protests and departure of the United States Navy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Protests and departure of the United States Navy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_in_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="United States Navy in Vieques, Puerto Rico">United States Navy in Vieques, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Radar_in_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Radar_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Radar in Vieques, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The continuing postwar presence in Vieques of the United States Navy drew protests from the local community, angry at the expropriation of their land and the environmental impact of weapons testing. The locals\' discontent was exacerbated by the island\'s perilous economic condition.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Fuera_la_Marina_de_Vieques_Ya%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fuera la Marina de Vieques Ya</i></span> (translation: Navy out of Vieques now) sign on structure</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Protests came to a head in 1999 when Vieques native <a href="/wiki/David_Sanes" class="mw-redirect" title="David Sanes">David Sanes</a>, a civilian employee of the United States Navy, was killed by a jet bomb that the Navy said misfired. Sanes had been working as a security guard. A popular campaign of <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a> resurged; not since the mid-1970s had <i>Viequenses</i> come together <i>en masse</i> to protest the target practices.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The locals took to the ocean in their small fishing boats and successfully stopped the US Navy\'s military exercises for a short period, until the US Navy and two <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">US Coast Guard</a> cutters began controlling access to the island and escorting boaters away from Vieques.\n</p><p>On April 27, 2001, the Navy resumed operations and protesting resumed.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At this point over 600 protesters had already been detained.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Vieques issue became something of a <i><a href="/wiki/Cause_c%C3%A9l%C3%A8bre" title="Cause c\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa8bre">cause c\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa8bre</a></i>, and local protesters were joined by sympathetic groups and prominent individuals from the mainland United States and abroad, including political leaders <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Berr%C3%ADos" title="Rub\xc3\xa9n Berr\xc3\xados">Rub\xc3\xa9n Berr\xc3\xados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Kennedy, Jr.">Robert F. Kennedy Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Sharpton" title="Al Sharpton">Al Sharpton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rev._Jesse_Jackson" class="mw-redirect" title="Rev. Jesse Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a>, singers <a href="/wiki/Danny_Rivera" title="Danny Rivera">Danny Rivera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Col%C3%B3n" title="Willie Col\xc3\xb3n">Willie Col\xc3\xb3n</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, actors <a href="/wiki/Edward_James_Olmos" title="Edward James Olmos">Edward James Olmos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Smits" title="Jimmy Smits">Jimmy Smits</a>, boxer <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Trinidad" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Trinidad">F\xc3\xa9lix \'Tito\' Trinidad</a>, baseball superstar <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Delgado" title="Carlos Delgado">Carlos Delgado</a>, writers <a href="/wiki/Ana_Lydia_Vega" title="Ana Lydia Vega">Ana Lydia Vega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Braschi" title="Giannina Braschi">Giannina Braschi</a>, and Guatemala\'s Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Rigoberta_Mench%C3%BA" title="Rigoberta Mench\xc3\xba">Rigoberta Mench\xc3\xba</a>. Kennedy\'s son, Aidan Caohman "Vieques" Kennedy,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> was born while his father served jail time in Puerto Rico for his role in the protests. The problems arising from the US Navy base have also featured in songs by various musicians, including Puerto Rican rock band <a href="/wiki/Puya_(band)" title="Puya (band)">Puya</a>, rapper <a href="/wiki/Immortal_Technique" title="Immortal Technique">Immortal Technique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">reggaeton</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Tego_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Tego Calder\xc3\xb3n">Tego Calder\xc3\xb3n</a>. In popular culture, one <a href="/wiki/Subplot" title="Subplot">subplot</a> of "<a href="/wiki/The_Two_Bartlets" class="mw-redirect" title="The Two Bartlets">The Two Bartlets</a>" episode of <a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a> dealt with a protest on the bombing range led by a friend of <a href="/wiki/White_House_Deputy_Chief_of_Staff" title="White House Deputy Chief of Staff">White House Deputy Chief of Staff</a> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Lyman" title="Josh Lyman">Josh Lyman</a>; the character was modeled on future West Wing star <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Smits" title="Jimmy Smits">Jimmy Smits</a>, a native of Puerto Rico who was repeatedly arrested for leading protests there.\n</p><p>As a result of this pressure, in May 2003 the Navy withdrew from Vieques, and much of the island was designated a <a href="/wiki/National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="National Wildlife Refuge">National Wildlife Refuge</a> under the control of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The island was also placed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Priorities_List" title="National Priorities List">National Priorities List</a> (NPL), the list of hazardous waste sites in the United States eligible for long-term remedial action (cleanup) financed by the federal Superfund program. Closure of <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Roads_Naval_Station" title="Roosevelt Roads Naval Station">Roosevelt Roads Naval Station</a> followed in 2004, and prior to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> the Roosevelt Roads Naval Station was reopened.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hurricane_Maria_and_rebuilding_efforts">Hurricane Maria and rebuilding efforts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria and rebuilding efforts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mangroves_in_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/220px-Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/330px-Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/440px-Mangroves_in_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Mangroves in Vieques, where electrical power lines were destroyed by Hurricane Maria in 2017</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Puerto Rico was struck by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, and the storm caused widespread devastation and a near-total shutdown of the island\'s tourism-based economy. The largest hotel on the island, <i>The W,</i> has not reopened since the storm, but most smaller hotels, bed and breakfasts, and Airbnb operators have resumed operations.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of December 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Susana_Centeno_Hospital" title="Susana Centeno Hospital">Susana Centeno Hospital</a> in Vieques had not been repaired and remained shuttered. Expectant mothers had to travel to the main island of Puerto Rico to give birth. People needing dialysis had to travel to the main island. In November 2018, a mobile dialysis machine was delivered to a temporary clinic.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 21, 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) approved $39.5&#160;million to help rebuild its only hospital after damage caused by Hurricane Maria. FEMA approved the funding after the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">Office of Management and Budget</a> agreed to provide money to rebuild the Susan Centeno community health center based on its "replacement value."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The family of Jaideliz Moreno Ventura, 13, whose 2020 death was blamed on the lack of a functioning hospital and lifesaving medical equipment in Vieques, is suing the government for violation of human and civil rights. Funds for rebuilding the hospital were approved two weeks after Jaideliz\'s death, but as of January 31, 2021, it has not been rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>While <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Pierluisi" title="Pedro Pierluisi">Governor Pedro Pierluisi</a> expected construction to begin on the hospital rebuild in 2022,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> it was delayed until 2023 with the holdup blamed on both construction complications on the island and further bureaucratic proceduress by <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">FEMA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda,_Vieques_PR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg/200px-Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg/300px-Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg/400px-Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_Isabel_Segunda%2C_Vieques_PR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_de_Vieques" title="Casa Alcald\xc3\xada de Vieques">Casa Alcald\xc3\xada</a> (City Hall), Isabel Segunda</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">Government of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Vieques is a <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipio of Puerto Rico</a>, translated as "municipality" and in this context roughly equivalent to "township". It is in the Puerto Rican electoral district of Carolina. Local government is under the leadership of a mayor, presently Junito Corcino.\n</p><p>Vieques belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VIII">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VIII</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_A._Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Pedro A. Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Pedro A. Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Daniel_Rivera" title="Luis Daniel Rivera">Luis Daniel Rivera</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vieques_Barrios.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Vieques_Barrios.jpg/500px-Vieques_Barrios.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="191" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Vieques_Barrios.jpg/750px-Vieques_Barrios.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Vieques_Barrios.jpg/1000px-Vieques_Barrios.jpg 2x" data-file-width="14096" data-file-height="5376" /></a><figcaption>Topographic Map of Vieques, 1951<br />with <i><a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a></i></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Vieques is divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>, including the downtown barrio called Isabel Segunda.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1226773818">.mw-parser-output title="Llave">Llave</a>\n</th>\n<td>15420815</td>\n<td>8</td>\n<td>0.5</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x94\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Mosquito,_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mosquito, Vieques, Puerto Rico">Mosquito</a>\n</th>\n<td>6279364</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0.0</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x94\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Diablo" title="Puerto Diablo">Puerto Diablo</a>\n</th>\n<td>45323702</td>\n<td>984</td>\n<td>21.7</td>\n<td>Roca Cucaracha, Isla Yallis, Roca Alcatraz, Cayo Conejo, Cayo Jalovita, Cayo Jalova\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ferro" title="Puerto Ferro">Puerto Ferro</a>\n</th>\n<td>21199791</td>\n<td>856</td>\n<td>40.4</td>\n<td>Isla Chiva, Cayo Chiva\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Real,_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Real, Vieques, Puerto Rico">Puerto Real</a>\n</th>\n<td>19943599</td>\n<td>1673</td>\n<td>83.9</td>\n<td>Cayo de Tierra, Cayo de Afuera (Cayo Real)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas,_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Punta Arenas, Vieques, Puerto Rico">Punta Arenas</a>\n</th>\n<td>11227244</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0.0</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x94\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#EAECF0; font-weight:bold;" class="sortbottom">\n<th scope="row" style="background:#EAECF0; font-weight:bold;">Vieques\n</th>\n<td>131645368</td>\n<td>9106</td>\n<td>69.2</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Vieques, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Vieques, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Vieques: Sector Gobeo in Barrio Florida, Bravos de Boston, \nJag\xc3\xbceyes, Monte Carmelo, Pozo Prieto (Monte Santo) and Villa Borinqu\xc3\xa9n.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg/300px-Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg/450px-Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg/600px-Sub-tropical_dry_forest_vieques.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Sub-tropical dry forest on Vieques</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Vieques measures about 21 miles (34&#160;km) east-west, and three to four miles (6.4&#160;km) north-south. It has a land area of 52 square miles (130&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and is located about ten miles (16&#160;km) to the east of Puerto Rico. To the north of Vieques is the Atlantic Ocean, and to the south, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean</a>. The island of <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a> is about 10 miles (16&#160;km) north of Vieques, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> lie to the east. Vieques and Culebra, together with various small islets, make up the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Virgin_Islands" title="Spanish Virgin Islands">Spanish Virgin Islands</a>, sometimes known as the Passage Islands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The former US Navy lands, now wildlife reserves, occupy the entire eastern and western ends of Vieques, with the former live weapons testing site (known as the "LIA", or "Live Impact Area") at the extreme eastern tip.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These areas are unpopulated. The former civilian area occupies very roughly the central third of the island and contains the towns of <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Segunda,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabel Segunda, Puerto Rico">Isabel Segunda</a> on the north coast, and <a href="/wiki/Esperanza,_Puerto_Rico" title="Esperanza, Puerto Rico">Esperanza</a> on the south.\n</p><p>Vieques has a terrain of rolling hills, with a central ridge running east\xe2\x80\x93west. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Monte_Pirata_(Vieques)" title="Monte Pirata (Vieques)">Monte Pirata</a> at 987 feet (301&#160;m). Geologically the island is composed of a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_rock" title="Volcanic rock">volcanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Bedrock" title="Bedrock">bedrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">alluvial deposits</a> of gravel, sand, silt, and clay. There are no permanent rivers or streams. Much former agricultural land has been reclaimed by nature due to prolonged disuse, and, apart from some small-scale farming in the central region, the island is largely covered by brush and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_dry_forests" title="Puerto Rican dry forests">subtropical dry forest</a>. Around the coast lie palm-fringed sandy beaches interspersed with lagoons, <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove swamps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt flats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>A series of nearshore islets and rocks are part of the municipality of Vieques, clockwise starting at the northernmost:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Roca Cucaracha (a rock of less than five meters in diameter)</li>\n<li>Isla Yallis</li>\n<li>Roca Alcatraz</li>\n<li>Cayo Conejo</li>\n<li>Cayo Jalovita</li>\n<li>Cayo Jalova</li>\n<li>Isla Chiva</li>\n<li>Cayo Chiva</li>\n<li>Cayo de Tierra</li>\n<li>Cayo de Afuera (Cayo Real)</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bioluminescent_Bay">Bioluminescent Bay</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bioluminescent Bay"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" /></video></span><figcaption>Kayaking in <a href="#Bioluminescent_Bay">the Bioluminescent Bay</a>, Vieques, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Mosquito" title="Puerto Mosquito">Puerto Mosquito</a></div>\n<p>The Vieques <a href="/wiki/Bioluminescence" title="Bioluminescence">Bioluminescent</a> Bay (also known as <i>Puerto Mosquito</i>, <i>Mosquito Bay</i>, or <i>"The Bio Bay"</i>), was declared the "Brightest bioluminescent bay" in the world by <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is listed as a <a href="/wiki/National_natural_landmark" class="mw-redirect" title="National natural landmark">national natural landmark</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Natural_Landmarks_in_Puerto_Rico" title="List of National Natural Landmarks in Puerto Rico">five in Puerto Rico</a>. The luminescence in the bay is caused by a <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dinoflagellate" title="Dinoflagellate">dinoflagellate</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pyrodinium_bahamense" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyrodinium bahamense">Pyrodinium bahamense</a></i>, which glows whenever the water is disturbed, leaving a trail of neon blue.\n</p><p>A combination of factors creates the necessary conditions for bioluminescence: <a href="/wiki/Rhizophora_mangle" title="Rhizophora mangle">red mangrove</a> trees surround the water (the organisms have been related to mangrove forests<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although mangrove is not necessarily associated with this species<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>); a complete lack of modern development around the bay; the water is warm enough and deep enough; and a small channel to the ocean keeps the <a href="/wiki/Dinoflagellate" title="Dinoflagellate">dinoflagellates</a> in the bay. This small channel was created artificially, the result of attempts by the occupants of Spanish ships to choke off the bay from the ocean. The Spanish believed that the bioluminescence they encountered there while first exploring the area was the work of the <a href="/wiki/Devil" title="Devil">devil</a> and tried to block ocean water from entering the bay by dropping huge boulders in the channel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Spanish only succeeded in preserving and increasing the luminescence in the now isolated bay.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kayaking" title="Kayaking">Kayaking</a> is permitted in the bay and may be arranged through local vendors.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Vieques has a warm, relatively dry, tropical climate. Temperatures vary little throughout the year, with average daily maxima ranging from 84.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F (29.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in January to 89.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F (32.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in September. Average daily minima are about 18&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 6&#160;\xc2\xb0C lower. Rainfall averages around 40 to 45 inches (1,000 to 1,100 millimetres) per year, with the month of September being the wettest. The west of the island receives significantly more rainfall than the east. Prevailing winds are easterly.\n</p><p>Vieques is prone to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storms</a> and at risk from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">hurricanes</a> from June to November. In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> caused considerable damage to the island,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> also caused major damage.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for Vieques Island, Puerto Rico (1955\xe2\x80\x931976 normals,
