href="#cite_note-US2010Census-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n2020<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2020">2020</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2020"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>According to the 2020 Census, Vieques is the third-least populous municipality (after <a href="/wiki/Maricao" class="mw-redirect" title="Maricao">Maricao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>) with a population of 8,249.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>8.0% of the population is of non-Hispanic origin, making it the second-least Hispanic municipality in Puerto Rico after <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>. This represents an increase from 2010, when only 5.7% of the population was non-Hispanic.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2010">2010</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2010"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The 2010 US census,<sup id="cite_ref-census_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> showed the total population of Vieques was 9,301. 94.3% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race). Natives of Vieques are known as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Viequenses</i></span>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3">Self-defined race 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnicity_2010_census_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnicity_2010_census-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Race\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>% of population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/White_Puerto_Ricans" title="White Puerto Ricans">White</a></b></td>\n<td>5,456</td>\n<td>48.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Afro-Puerto_Rican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Puerto Rican">Black</a></b></td>\n<td>2,617</td>\n<td>38.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> <br />and <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a></b></td>\n<td>62</td>\n<td>0.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a></b></td>\n<td>6</td>\n<td>0.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Hawaiian">Native Hawaiian</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a></b></td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Some other race</b></td>\n<td>688</td>\n<td>7.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Two or more races</b></td>\n<td>309</td>\n<td>3.4\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Language">Language</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Language"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Spanish" title="Puerto Rican Spanish">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">English</a> are recognized as official languages. Spanish is the primary language of most inhabitants.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sugar_industry" title="Sugar industry">sugar industry</a>, once the mainstay of the island\'s economy, declined during the early 20th century, and finally collapsed in the 1940s when the US Navy took over much of the land on which the sugar cane plantations stood. After an initial naval construction phase, opportunities to make a living on the island were increased to include not only fishing or subsistence farming, but also Naval jobs. Crops grown on the island include <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocados</a>, bananas, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>, grains, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papayas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>. A number of permanent local jobs were provided by the US Navy, and their economy benefited. Starting in the 1970s <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> had employed a few hundred workers at a manufacturing plant but that plant subsequently closed.  Unemployment was widespread, with consequent social problems. The 2000 US census reported a median household income in 1999 dollars of $9,331 (compared to $41,994 for the US as a whole), and 35.8% of the population of 16 years and over in the labor force (compared to 63.9% for the US as a whole).<sup id="cite_ref-census_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the 2003 departure of the US Navy, the frail economy of the island was left in shambles, and efforts had to be made to redevelop the island\'s agricultural economy, clean up contaminated areas of the former bombing ranges, and to develop Vieques as a tourist destination. The Navy cleanup is now the island\'s largest employer, and has contributed over $20&#160;million to the local economy over the last five years through salaries, housing, vehicles, taxes, and services. The Navy has provided specialized training to several local islanders.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Corcho_Beach,_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Corcho_Beach%2C_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Corcho_Beach%2C_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="194" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Corcho_Beach%2C_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/450px-Corcho_Beach%2C_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0b/Corcho_Beach%2C_Vieques%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="504" data-file-height="326" /></a><figcaption>Bah\xc3\xada del Corcho (Cork Bay), or Playa Caracas (Caracas Beach), also called Red Beach, a name given to the beach by the U.S. Navy and used mostly by English speakers</figcaption></figure>\n<p>For sixty years the majority of Vieques was closed off by the US Navy, and the island remained almost entirely undeveloped for tourism. This lack of development is now marketed as a key attraction. Vieques is promoted under an <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> banner as a sleepy, unspoiled island of rural bucolic charm and pristine deserted beaches, and is rapidly becoming a popular destination.\n</p><p>Since the Navy\'s departure, tensions on the island have been low, although land speculation by foreign developers and fears of overdevelopment have caused some resentment among local residents, and there are occasional reports of lingering <a href="/wiki/Anti-Americanism" title="Anti-Americanism">anti-American sentiment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boston_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boston-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The lands previously owned by the Navy have been turned over to the U.S. National Fish and Wildlife Service and the authorities of Puerto Rico and Vieques for management. The immediate bombing range area on the eastern tip of the island suffers from severe contamination, but the remaining areas are mostly open to the public, including many beautiful beaches that were inaccessible to civilians while the military was conducting training maneuvers.\n</p><p>Snorkeling is excellent, especially at <a href="/wiki/Blue_Beach_(Vieques)" title="Blue Beach (Vieques)">Blue Beach</a> (Bah\xc3\xada de la Chiva). Aside from archeological sites, such as La Hueca, and deserted beaches, a unique feature of Vieques is the presence of two pristine <a href="/wiki/Bioluminescence" title="Bioluminescence">bioluminescent</a> bays, including Mosquito Bay. Vieques is also famous for its <a href="/wiki/Paso_fino" class="mw-redirect" title="Paso fino">paso fino</a> horses, which are owned by locals and left to roam free over parts of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Boston_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boston-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/TripAdvisor" class="mw-redirect" title="TripAdvisor">TripAdvisor</a> listed Vieques among the Top 25 Beaches in the World, writing "If you prefer your beaches without the accompanying commercial developments, Isla de Vieques is your tanning turf, with more than 40 beaches and not one traffic light."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of summer 2020, travel to the island was restricted due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a> <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">outbreak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Ceiba_tree_in_Vieques_Island%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Very old Ceiba tree in Vieques Island, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fuerte_de_Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuerte de Vieques">Fort\xc3\xadn Conde de Mirasol</a> (Count Mirasol Fort), a fort built by the Spanish in the mid 19th century, now a museum</li>\n<li>Playa Esperanza (<a href="/wiki/Esperanza_Beach" title="Esperanza Beach">Esperanza Beach</a>)</li>\n<li>The tomb of Le Guillou, the town founder, in <a href="/wiki/Isabel_II_barrio-pueblo" title="Isabel II barrio-pueblo">Isabel Segunda</a></li>\n<li>La Casa Alcald\xc3\xada (City Hall)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Mulas_Light" title="Punta Mulas Light">Faro Punta Mulas</a>, built in 1896</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ferro_Light" title="Puerto Ferro Light">Faro de Puerto Ferro</a></li>\n<li>Sun Bay Beach<sup id="cite_ref-Sun_Bay_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sun_Bay-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The Bioluminescent Bay</li>\n<li>The 300-year-old <a href="/wiki/Ceiba" title="Ceiba">ceiba</a> tree</li>\n<li>Rompeolas (Mosquito Pier), renamed Puerto de la Libertad <a href="/wiki/David_Sanes" class="mw-redirect" title="David Sanes">David Sanes Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> in 2003</li>\n<li>Puerto Ferro Archaeological Site</li>\n<li>Black Sand Beach (Playa Negra)</li>\n<li>Hacienda Playa Grande (Old Sugarcane Plantation Building)</li>\n<li>Underground U.S. Navy Bunkers<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Wreckage of the World War II Navy Destroyer <a href="/wiki/USS_Killen" title="USS Killen">USS&#160;<i>Killen</i>&#160;(DD-593)</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg/200px-20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg/300px-20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg/400px-20080720_155752_Festival_Viequense_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="638" /></a><figcaption>Fiestas Patronales, Isabel Segunda, 2008</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Vieques celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in July. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Carmen</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Vieques include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Three Kings Festival \xe2\x80\x93 (or <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany Festival</a>) \xe2\x80\x93 January 6</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival Cultural Viequense</i></span> (Vieques Cultural Festival) \xe2\x80\x93 June</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival de la Arepa</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 August/September</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Vieques flag, approved in 1975, contains a representation of the municipal coat of arms and maintains its same symbolism. It consists of seven horizontal straight stripes, of equal width, four white and three blue, alternated. In its center is a green rhombus where a simplified design of the castle appears in yellow. The naval crown seen on the coat of arms is omitted from the flag.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>On a barry shield with silver and blue waves is a <a href="/wiki/Vert_(heraldry)" title="Vert (heraldry)">green</a> rhombus with a gold castle and on top is a golden crown with silver sails. The silver and blue waves symbolize the sea around Vieques. In the green rhombus is a historic Vieques fort represented by the traditional Spanish heraldic castle.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Vieques is served by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Rivera_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Airport" title="Antonio Rivera Rodr\xc3\xadguez Airport">Antonio Rivera Rodr\xc3\xadguez Airport</a>, which currently accommodates only small propeller-driven aircraft. Services to the island run from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport">Isla Grande Airport</a> (20- to 30-minute flights) and from <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Aponte_de_la_Torre_Airport" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Aponte de la Torre Airport">Ceiba Airport</a> (5-minute flights) and to <a href="/wiki/Benjam%C3%ADn_Rivera_Noriega_Airport" title="Benjam\xc3\xadn Rivera Noriega Airport">Culebra</a>. Flights are also available between Vieques and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda" title="Virgin Gorda">Virgin Gorda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>.\n</p><p>Also, a <a href="/wiki/Vieques_Ferry" title="Vieques Ferry">ferry</a> runs from <a href="/wiki/Ceiba,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ceiba, Puerto Rico">Ceiba</a> several times a day. The ferry service is administered by the Autoridad de Transporte Mar\xc3\xadtimo (ATM) in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2019, governor <a href="/wiki/Wanda_V%C3%A1zquez_Garced" title="Wanda V\xc3\xa1zquez Garced">Wanda V\xc3\xa1zquez Garced</a> said she would address the troubled, inconsistent ferry service between the islands and Ceiba.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There are 13 bridges in Vieques, none of them distinguished.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Public_health">Public health</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Public health"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236091366">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2022</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>There have been claims linking Vieques\' higher cancer rate<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to the long history of weapons testing on the island.\n</p><p>Nayda Figueroa, an epidemiologist for Puerto Rico\'s Cancer Registry, stated that research showed Vieques\' cancer rate from 1995 to 1999 was 31 percent higher than for the main island.  <a href="/wiki/Michael_Thun" title="Michael Thun">Michael Thun</a>, head of epidemiological research at the American Cancer Society, cautioned that the variations in the rates could be attributed to chance, given the small population on Vieques.<sup id="cite_ref-MiamiHerald_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiamiHerald-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> \nA 2000 <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Regulatory_Commission" title="Nuclear Regulatory Commission">Nuclear Regulatory Commission</a> report concluded that "the public had not been exposed to depleted uranium contamination above normal background (naturally occurring) levels".<sup id="cite_ref-ATSDR_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATSDR-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Surveys of the wreckage of a target ship in a shallow bay at the bombing range, however, revealed its identity to be that of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Killen" title="USS Killen">USS&#160;<i>Killen</i></a>, a target ship in nuclear tests in the Pacific in 1958. By 2002, it was evident that thousands of tons of steel that had originally been irradiated in the 1958 nuclear tests was missing from the wreckage in the bay. That steel has been missing for over 35 years and is still unaccounted for by the US Navy, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> and US <a href="/wiki/Agency_for_Toxic_Substances_and_Disease_Registry" title="Agency for Toxic Substances and Disease Registry">Agency for Toxic Substances and Disease Registry</a> (ATSDR). Hundreds of steel drums of unknown origin were found among the wreckage. Their identity and contents have not been adequately verified.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In response to concerns about potential contamination from toxic metals and other chemicals, the ATSDR conducted a number of surveys in 1999\xe2\x80\x932002 to test Vieques\' soil, water supply, air, fish and shellfish for harmful substances. The general conclusion of the ATSDR survey was that no public health hazard existed as a result of the Navy\'s activities.<sup id="cite_ref-ATSDR_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATSDR-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, scientists have pointed out that fish samples were drawn from local markets, which often import fish from other areas. Also sample sizes from each location were too small to provide compelling evidence for the lack of a public health danger (Wargo, Green Intelligence). The conclusions of the ATSDR report have more recently, as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, been questioned and discredited. A review is underway.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Casa Pueblo, a Puerto Rican environmental group, reported "a series of studies pertaining to the flora and fauna of Vieques that clearly demonstrates sequestration of high levels of toxic elements in plant and animal tissue samples. Consequently, the ecological food web of the Vieques Island has been adversely impacted."<sup id="cite_ref-CasaPueblo_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CasaPueblo-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vieques,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable people"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jaime_Rexach_Benitez" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaime Rexach Benitez">Jaime Rexach Benitez</a>, educator, politician and humanist;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Susana_Centeno" title="Susana Centeno">Susana Centeno</a>, nurse, public servant</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Dieppa" title="Nelson Dieppa">Nelson Dieppa</a>, professional boxer;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Francisco_Luis" title="Juan Francisco Luis">Juan Francisco Luis</a>, Governor of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a> (1978\xe2\x80\x931987);</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/German_Rieckehoff" class="mw-redirect" title="German Rieckehoff">Germ\xc3\xa1n Rieckehoff Sampayo</a>, was president of the Puerto Rican Olympic committee;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_V%C3%A9lez_Rieckehoff" title="Carlos V\xc3\xa9lez Rieckehoff">Carlos V\xc3\xa9lez Rieckehoff</a>, local nationalist leader and political activist;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Sanes" class="mw-redirect" title="David Sanes">David Sanes Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>, civilian killed by the US Navy in a live-fire bombing practice, his death sparked protests that culminated in the US Navy leaving the island.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading
